It stripes a large index across a fleet of Meilisearch nodes, fans out search queries across all shards, merges ranked results, and rebalances shard assignments when nodes are added or removed — all without Meilisearch Enterprise.\n5\t\n6\t---\n7\t\n8\t## Table of Contents\n9\t\n10\t1. Design Principles\n29\t\n30\t1. **Invisible federation** — clients talk to one endpoint using the standard Meilisearch API. The sharding topology is entirely hidden. No SDK changes, no query changes, no schema changes.\n31\t2. **No Enterprise dependency** — all functionality is built on Meilisearch Community Edition (MIT licensed).\n32\t3. **Rendezvous hashing** — same algorithm Meilisearch Enterprise uses internally; minimal reshuffling on topology change, natural RF > 1 support.\n33\t4. **RF-configurable redundancy** — RF=1 for maximum capacity, RF=2 for one-node-loss tolerance, RF=3 for two-node-loss tolerance.\n34\t5. **Graceful degradation** — when a shard is unavailable, return partial results with a clear header rather than failing the entire request.\n35\t6. **Static binaries, scratch images** — musl compilation + scratch Docker base for minimal attack surface and trivial deployment.\n36\t7. **GitOps first** — all deployment configuration committed to `jedarden/declarative-config`; ArgoCD drives all cluster changes.\n37\t8. **Fixed per-pod resource envelope** — each Miroir orchestrator pod fits within **2 vCPU / 3.75 GB RAM**. When aggregate workload exceeds this envelope, scale **horizontally** by adding pods, never vertically beyond the envelope. The request path is strictly stateless; background work partitions across pods via shard-partitioned ownership, leader election, or a shared job queue. See Section 14.\n38\t\n39\t### Key constraints\n40\t\n41\t- **Logical shard count (S) is fixed at index creation** — this is the granularity of the hash space, not the number of physical machines. It determines how finely the keyspace is divided. Changing S requires a full reindex. Choose generously, per group: `S = max_nodes_per_group_ever × 8`. S is scoped to a single replica group because rendezvous assignment runs within each group independently (see Section 2); adding groups multiplies throughput without consuming additional S headroom.\n42\t- **Node count (N) is fully elastic** — nodes can be added or removed at any time without a full reindex. Adding a node to a group migrates only the `~1/(Ng+1)` fraction of that group's documents whose shard assignments change, where Ng is the number of nodes in the affected group. Documents in other groups are untouched. Removing a node migrates only that node's documents to surviving nodes within its own group. The rest of the corpus is untouched.\n43\t- All Meilisearch nodes must have **identical index settings** at all times. Miroir enforces this by broadcasting settings atomically.\n44\t- Documents **must** have an explicit primary key declared at index creation. Miroir cannot shard-route without it.\n45\t\n46\t---\n47\t\n48\t## 2. Architecture\n49\t\n50\t### Core model\n51\t\n52\tMiroir treats a fleet of Meilisearch CE instances the way software RAID treats a disk array, with an additional dimension for read throughput: **replica groups**.\n53\t\n54\t- The logical index is divided into **S shards** — a fixed hash-space granularity chosen at index creation\n55\t- The node fleet is divided into **RG replica groups** — independent pools each holding a complete copy of all shards\n56\t- Within each group, each shard is held by **RF nodes** (intra-group replication factor, for HA within the group)\n57\t- Every write fans out to all `RG × RF` target nodes (one per shard per group replica)\n58\t- Every search query is routed to exactly **one replica group** — the query fans out only to that group's covering set, not the entire fleet\n59\t- Read throughput scales with RG: doubling the groups doubles query capacity\n60\t- Storage capacity scales with total nodes: adding a node to a group reduces each node's share within that group\n61\t- The **node fleet is elastic**: nodes can be added to existing groups (capacity scaling) or new groups can be added (throughput scaling), both without a full reindex\n62\t- When the fleet topology changes, the orchestrator rebalances only the affected shards within the affected group\n63\t\n64\t```\n65\tClient\n66\t  │\n67\t  ▼\n68\tMiroir Orchestrator\n69\t  ├── Write path: hash(doc_id) → shard → fan out to RF nodes in EACH group (RG × RF total)\n70\t  ├── Read path:  pick one group → scatter to that group's covering set → merge results\n71\t  └── Rebalance: on node add/remove within a group → migrate minimum shards within that group\n72\t\n73\t  Replica Group 0              Replica Group 1\n74\t  ┌──────────────────┐        ┌──────────────────┐\n75\t  │ node-0  node-1   │        │ node-3  node-4   │     ...  (RG groups)\n76\t  │ node-2           │        │ node-5           │\n77\t  └──────────────────┘        └──────────────────┘\n78\t  (each group holds all S shards, distributed across its nodes)\n79\t```\n80\t\n81\t### Replication factor\n82\t\n83\t| RF | Redundancy | Node failures tolerated | Capacity |\n84\t|----|-----------|------------------------|----------|\n85\t| 1  | None (stripe only) | 0 | 100% of fleet |\n86\t| 2  | One replica | 1 per shard group | 50% of fleet |\n87\t| 3  | Two replicas | 2 per shard group | 33% of fleet |\n88\t\n89\t### Shard routing — Rendezvous hashing (HRW) within groups\n90\t\n91\tMiroir uses **Rendezvous hashing (HRW)** to assign shards to nodes. The assignment is scoped **within each replica group** — the rendezvous hash picks the top-RF nodes from a group's node list, not the global node list. This guarantees that every group independently forms a complete covering set with no cross-group shard overlap.\n92\t\n93\t```\n94\tnodes_in_group(g)           → the subset of nodes belonging to replica group g\n95\tassign_shard(shard_id, g)   → top RF nodes from nodes_in_group(g)\n96\t                              by score(hash(shard_id || node_id))\n97\t\n98\twrite_targets(shard_id)     → [assign_shard(shard_id, g) for g in 0..RG]\n99\t                              (flat union across all groups — RG × RF nodes total)"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4ebbb998-c656-45b5-9b13-5384c0aa2ecb","uuid":"41f148fc-c74a-48c2-9a59-3e2cb3e783da","timestamp":"2026-05-13T22:16:00.972Z","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/home/coding/miroir/docs/plan/plan.md","content":"# Miroir — Implementation Plan\n\n**Multi-node Index Replication Orchestrator, Integrated Rebalancing**\n\nMiroir is a RAID-like sharding and high-availability layer for Meilisearch Community Edition. It stripes a large index across a fleet of Meilisearch nodes, fans out search queries across all shards, merges ranked results, and rebalances shard assignments when nodes are added or removed — all without Meilisearch Enterprise.\n\n---\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Design Principles](#1-design-principles)\n2. [Architecture](#2-architecture)\n3. [Document, Index, and Search Lifecycle](#3-document-index-and-search-lifecycle)\n4. [Implementation](#4-implementation)\n5. [API Surface and Compatibility](#5-api-surface-and-compatibility)\n6. [Deployment](#6-deployment)\n7. [CI/CD](#7-cicd)\n8. [Testing](#8-testing)\n9. [Secrets Handling](#9-secrets-handling)\n10. [Observability](#10-observability)\n11. [Onboarding](#11-onboarding)\n12. [Delivered Artifacts](#12-delivered-artifacts)\n13. [Advanced Capabilities](#13-advanced-capabilities)\n14. [Resource Envelope and Horizontal Scaling](#14-resource-envelope-and-horizontal-scaling)\n15. [Open Problems](#15-open-problems)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Design Principles\n\n1. **Invisible federation** — clients talk to one endpoint using the standard Meilisearch API. The sharding topology is entirely hidden. No SDK changes, no query changes, no schema changes.\n2. **No Enterprise dependency** — all functionality is built on Meilisearch Community Edition (MIT licensed).\n3. **Rendezvous hashing** — same algorithm Meilisearch Enterprise uses internally; minimal reshuffling on topology change, natural RF > 1 support.\n4. **RF-configurable redundancy** — RF=1 for maximum capacity, RF=2 for one-node-loss tolerance, RF=3 for two-node-loss tolerance.\n5. **Graceful degradation** — when a shard is unavailable, return partial results with a clear header rather than failing the entire request.\n6. **Static binaries, scratch images** — musl compilation + scratch Docker base for minimal attack surface and trivial deployment.\n7. **GitOps first** — all deployment configuration committed to `jedarden/declarative-config`; ArgoCD drives all cluster changes.\n8. **Fixed per-pod resource envelope** — each Miroir orchestrator pod fits within **2 vCPU / 3.75 GB RAM**. When aggregate workload exceeds this envelope, scale **horizontally** by adding pods, never vertically beyond the envelope. The request path is strictly stateless; background work partitions across pods via shard-partitioned ownership, leader election, or a shared job queue. See Section 14.\n\n### Key constraints\n\n- **Logical shard count (S) is fixed at index creation** — this is the granularity of the hash space, not the number of physical machines. It determines how finely the keyspace is divided. Changing S requires a full reindex. Choose generously, per group: `S = max_nodes_per_group_ever × 8`. S is scoped to a single replica group because rendezvous assignment runs within each group independently (see Section 2); adding groups multiplies throughput without consuming additional S headroom.\n- **Node count (N) is fully elastic** — nodes can be added or removed at any time without a full reindex. Adding a node to a group migrates only the `~1/(Ng+1)` fraction of that group's documents whose shard assignments change, where Ng is the number of nodes in the affected group. Documents in other groups are untouched. Removing a node migrates only that node's documents to surviving nodes within its own group. The rest of the corpus is untouched.\n- All Meilisearch nodes must have **identical index settings** at all times. Miroir enforces this by broadcasting settings atomically.\n- Documents **must** have an explicit primary key declared at index creation. Miroir cannot shard-route without it.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Architecture\n\n### Core model\n\nMiroir treats a fleet of Meilisearch CE instances the way software RAID treats a disk array, with an additional dimension for read throughput: **replica groups**.\n\n- The logical index is divided into **S shards** — a fixed hash-space granularity chosen at index creation\n- The node fleet is divided into **RG replica groups** — independent pools each holding a complete copy of all shards\n- Within each group, each shard is held by **RF nodes** (intra-group replication factor, for HA within the group)\n- Every write fans out to all `RG × RF` target nodes (one per shard per group replica)\n- Every search query is routed to exactly **one replica group** — the query fans out only to that group's covering set, not the entire fleet\n- Read throughput scales with RG: doubling the groups doubles query capacity\n- Storage capacity scales with total nodes: adding a node to a group reduces each node's share within that group\n- The **node fleet is elastic**: nodes can be added to existing groups (capacity scaling) or new groups can be added (throughput scaling), both without a full reindex\n- When the fleet topology changes, the orchestrator rebalances only the affected shards within the affected group\n\n```\nClient\n  │\n  ▼\nMiroir Orchestrator\n  ├── Write path: hash(doc_id) → shard → fan out to RF nodes in EACH group (RG × RF total)\n  ├── Read path:  pick one group → scatter to that group's covering set → merge results\n  └── Rebalance: on node add/remove within a group → migrate minimum shards within that group\n\n  Replica Group 0              Replica Group 1\n  ┌──────────────────┐        ┌──────────────────┐\n  │ node-0  node-1   │        │ node-3  node-4   │     ...  (RG groups)\n  │ node-2           │        │ node-5           │\n  └──────────────────┘        └──────────────────┘\n  (each group holds all S shards, distributed across its nodes)\n```\n\n### Replication factor\n\n| RF | Redundancy | Node failures tolerated | Capacity |\n|----|-----------|------------------------|----------|\n| 1  | None (stripe only) | 0 | 100% of fleet |\n| 2  | One replica | 1 per shard group | 50% of fleet |\n| 3  | Two replicas | 2 per shard group | 33% of fleet |\n\n### Shard routing — Rendezvous hashing (HRW) within groups\n\nMiroir uses **Rendezvous hashing (HRW)** to assign shards to nodes. The assignment is scoped **within each replica group** — the rendezvous hash picks the top-RF nodes from a group's node list, not the global node list. This guarantees that every group independently forms a complete covering set with no cross-group shard overlap.\n\n```\nnodes_in_group(g)           → the subset of nodes belonging to replica group g\nassign_shard(shard_id, g)   → top RF nodes from nodes_in_group(g)\n                              by score(hash(shard_id || node_id))\n\nwrite_targets(shard_id)     → [assign_shard(shard_id, g) for g in 0..RG]\n                              (flat union across all groups — RG × RF nodes total)","numLines":100,"startLine":0,"totalLines":3740}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"call_31e782a47005446c99d79a66","type":"tool_result","content":"530\t\n531\t### Task store schema (SQLite)\n532\t\n533\tThe task store persists all orchestrator state that must survive a pod restart. In single-replica deployments the backend is SQLite; in HA mode Redis replaces it (keyspace mapping below). Every table below is defined here and cross-referenced from the §13 / §14.5 section that consumes it.\n534\t\n535\t**1. `tasks` — Miroir task registry (defined here; consumed throughout §2, §3, §13).**\n536\t\n537\t```sql\n538\tCREATE TABLE tasks (\n539\t    miroir_id   TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n540\t    created_at  INTEGER NOT NULL,\n541\t    status      TEXT NOT NULL,   -- enqueued | processing | succeeded | failed | canceled\n542\t    node_tasks  TEXT NOT NULL,   -- JSON: {\"node-0\": 42, \"node-1\": 17}\n543\t    error       TEXT\n544\t);\n545\t```\n546\t\n547\tBackground Tokio tasks poll node task statuses and update rows. Old tasks are pruned after a TTL (default 7 days) by the rendezvous-partitioned pruner of §14.5 Mode A.\n548\t\n549\t**2. `node_settings_version` — per-(index, node) settings freshness (consumed by §13.5).**\n550\t\n551\t```sql\n552\tCREATE TABLE node_settings_version (\n553\t    index_uid   TEXT NOT NULL,\n554\t    node_id     TEXT NOT NULL,\n555\t    version     INTEGER NOT NULL,   -- last cluster-wide settings_version this (index, node) pair verified\n556\t    updated_at  INTEGER NOT NULL,\n557\t    PRIMARY KEY (index_uid, node_id)\n558\t);\n559\t```\n560\t\n561\tAdvanced whenever a two-phase verify (§13.5 Phase 2) or drift-repair cycle succeeds for that pair. Covering-set construction for reads carrying `X-Miroir-Min-Settings-Version` excludes rows where `version < floor`.\n562\t\n563\t**3. `aliases` — atomic index aliases (consumed by §13.7, extended for multi-target by §13.17).**\n564\t\n565\t```sql\n566\tCREATE TABLE aliases (\n567\t    name          TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n568\t    kind          TEXT NOT NULL,          -- 'single' | 'multi'\n569\t    current_uid   TEXT,                   -- non-null when kind='single'\n570\t    target_uids   TEXT,                   -- JSON array of UIDs; non-null when kind='multi'\n571\t    version       INTEGER NOT NULL,       -- monotonic flip counter\n572\t    created_at    INTEGER NOT NULL,\n573\t    history       TEXT NOT NULL           -- JSON array: last N prior states, bounded by aliases.history_retention\n574\t);\n575\t```\n576\t\n577\tTwo alias types are supported:\n578\t- **Single-target alias (`kind='single'`)** — one `current_uid`; client writes and reads both resolve to that UID; atomic flip via `PUT /_miroir/aliases/{name}`.\n579\t- **Multi-target alias (`kind='multi'`)** — `target_uids` is a JSON array of concrete UIDs; reads fan out across all of them via §13.11 multi-search and merge by `_rankingScore`; writes are rejected with `miroir_multi_alias_not_writable` (see §13.7). Multi-target aliases are managed exclusively by §13.17 ILM; direct operator edits are refused.\n580\t\n581\tAlias flips update `current_uid` (single) or `target_uids` (multi) and `version` atomically; `history` is append-only within the retention bound.\n582\t\n583\t**4. `sessions` — read-your-writes session pins (consumed by §13.6).**\n584\t\n585\t```sql\n586\tCREATE TABLE sessions (\n587\t    session_id            TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n588\t    last_write_mtask_id   TEXT,           -- nullable: session may exist before any write\n589\t    last_write_at         INTEGER,\n590\t    pinned_group          INTEGER,        -- group_id that first reached per-group quorum; nullable when pin cleared\n591\t    min_settings_version  INTEGER NOT NULL,\n592\t    ttl                   INTEGER NOT NULL -- expiry timestamp (ms since epoch); default 15m from last use\n593\t);\n594\t```\n595\t\n596\tLRU-bounded by `session_pinning.max_sessions`. Rows past `ttl` are evicted lazily on access.\n597\t\n598\t**5. `idempotency_cache` — write deduplication (consumed by §13.10).**\n599\t\n600\t```sql\n601\tCREATE TABLE idempotency_cache (\n602\t    key              TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n603\t    body_sha256      BLOB NOT NULL,\n604\t    miroir_task_id   TEXT NOT NULL,\n605\t    expires_at       INTEGER NOT NULL\n606\t);\n607\t```\n608\t\n609\tTTL defaults to 24h (`idempotency.ttl_seconds`). LRU-bounded by `idempotency.max_cached_keys`.\n610\t\n611\t**6. `jobs` — work-queued background jobs (consumed by §14.5 Mode C).**\n612\t\n613\t```sql\n614\tCREATE TABLE jobs (\n615\t    id                 TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n616\t    type               TEXT NOT NULL,   -- dump_import | reshard_backfill | ...\n617\t    params             TEXT NOT NULL,   -- JSON\n618\t    state              TEXT NOT NULL,   -- queued | in_progress | completed | failed\n619\t    claimed_by         TEXT,            -- pod_id of current claimant; nullable when queued\n620\t    claim_expires_at   INTEGER,         -- lease heartbeat expiry\n621\t    progress           TEXT NOT NULL    -- JSON: { bytes_processed, docs_routed, last_cursor, ... }\n622\t);\n623\t```\n624\t\n625\tClaim semantics and chunking rules are §14.5 Mode C.\n626\t\n627\t**7. `leader_lease` — singleton-coordinator lease (consumed by §14.5 Mode B).**\n628\t\n629\t```sql\n630\tCREATE TABLE leader_lease (\n631\t    scope        TEXT PRIMARY KEY,   -- e.g. \"reshard:<index>\", \"alias_flip:<name>\", \"settings_broadcast:<index>\"\n632\t    holder       TEXT NOT NULL,      -- pod_id of current leader\n633\t    expires_at   INTEGER NOT NULL    -- renewed every 3s with a 10s TTL\n634\t);\n635\t```\n636\t\n637\tFor SQLite deployments a single-replica advisory lock substitutes; the row is still written so recovery can read the last committed phase state after leader loss.\n638\t\n639\t**8. `canaries` — canary definitions (consumed by §13.18).**\n640\t\n641\t```sql\n642\tCREATE TABLE canaries (\n643\t    id             TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n644\t    name           TEXT NOT NULL,\n645\t    index_uid      TEXT NOT NULL,\n646\t    interval_s     INTEGER NOT NULL,\n647\t    query_json     TEXT NOT NULL,     -- JSON: the canary query body\n648\t    assertions_json TEXT NOT NULL,    -- JSON: array of assertion specs\n649\t    enabled        INTEGER NOT NULL,  -- 0 | 1\n650\t    created_at     INTEGER NOT NULL\n651\t);\n652\t```\n653\t\n654\tCreated and modified via `POST /_miroir/canaries`. The canary runner (Mode A, §14.5) reads this table on each scheduling tick.\n655\t\n656\t**9. `canary_runs` — canary run history (consumed by §13.18).**\n657\t\n658\t```sql\n659\tCREATE TABLE canary_runs (\n660\t    canary_id              TEXT NOT NULL,\n661\t    ran_at                 INTEGER NOT NULL,\n662\t    status                 TEXT NOT NULL,    -- pass | fail | error\n663\t    latency_ms             INTEGER NOT NULL,\n664\t    failed_assertions_json TEXT,             -- JSON array or NULL when pass\n665\t    PRIMARY KEY (canary_id, ran_at)\n666\t);\n667\t```\n668\t\n669\tBounded by `canary_runner.run_history_per_canary` (default 100) — older rows are pruned on insert.\n670\t\n671\t**10. `cdc_cursors` — per-sink per-index CDC cursor (consumed by §13.13).**\n672\t\n673\t```sql\n674\tCREATE TABLE cdc_cursors (\n675\t    sink_name       TEXT NOT NULL,\n676\t    index_uid       TEXT NOT NULL,\n677\t    last_event_seq  INTEGER NOT NULL,\n678\t    updated_at      INTEGER NOT NULL,\n679\t    PRIMARY KEY (sink_name, index_uid)\n680\t);\n681\t```\n682\t\n683\tAdvanced when a sink ACKs successful delivery of an event batch. `GET /_miroir/changes?since=…` reads against this same monotonic sequence. Shadow-diff state (§13.16) is explicitly **not** persisted — it lives in the in-memory ring buffer of size `shadow.diff_buffer_size`.\n684\t\n685\t**11. `tenant_map` — API-key → tenant mapping for `tenant_affinity.mode: api_key` (consumed by §13.15).**\n686\t\n687\t```sql\n688\tCREATE TABLE tenant_map (\n689\t    api_key_hash  BLOB PRIMARY KEY,   -- sha256(api_key)\n690\t    tenant_id     TEXT NOT NULL,\n691\t    group_id      INTEGER             -- nullable: NULL falls through to hash(tenant_id) % RG\n692\t);\n693\t```\n694\t\n695\tLoaded lazily on first request per key and cached per-pod. Only consulted when `tenant_affinity.mode: api_key`.\n696\t\n697\t**12. `rollover_policies` — ILM rollover policies (consumed by §13.17).**\n698\t\n699\t```sql\n700\tCREATE TABLE rollover_policies (\n701\t    name           TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n702\t    write_alias    TEXT NOT NULL,\n703\t    read_alias     TEXT NOT NULL,\n704\t    pattern        TEXT NOT NULL,      -- e.g. \"logs-{YYYY-MM-DD}\"\n705\t    triggers_json  TEXT NOT NULL,      -- JSON: { max_docs, max_age, max_size_gb }\n706\t    retention_json TEXT NOT NULL,      -- JSON: { keep_indexes }\n707\t    template_json  TEXT NOT NULL,      -- JSON: { primary_key, settings_ref }\n708\t    enabled        INTEGER NOT NULL    -- 0 | 1\n709\t);\n710\t```\n711\t\n712\tRead by the daily leader-coordinated ILM job (Mode B, §14.5) during each `ilm.check_interval_s` tick.\n713\t\n714\t**13. `search_ui_config` — per-index search-UI configuration (consumed by §13.21).**\n715\t\n716\t```sql\n717\tCREATE TABLE search_ui_config (\n718\t    index_uid    TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n719\t    config_json  TEXT NOT NULL,        -- JSON: the `search_ui:` entry as described in §13.21\n720\t    updated_at   INTEGER NOT NULL\n721\t);\n722\t```\n723\t\n724\tWritten by `POST /_miroir/ui/search/{index}/config`; read by the embedded SPA at page-load time.\n725\t\n726\t**14. `admin_sessions` — Admin UI session registry (consumed by §13.19 login/logout, §4 `/_miroir/admin/*`).**\n727\t\n728\t```sql\n729\tCREATE TABLE admin_sessions (\n730\t    session_id      TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n731\t    csrf_token      TEXT NOT NULL,\n732\t    admin_key_hash  TEXT NOT NULL,    -- sha256 of admin key used at login\n733\t    created_at      INTEGER NOT NULL,\n734\t    expires_at      INTEGER NOT NULL,\n735\t    revoked         INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,\n736\t    user_agent      TEXT,\n737\t    source_ip       TEXT\n738\t);\n739\tCREATE INDEX admin_sessions_expires ON admin_sessions(expires_at);\n740\t```\n741\t\n742\tWritten by `POST /_miroir/admin/login`; `revoked` is flipped to `1` by `POST /_miroir/admin/logout`. Every cookie-authenticated request re-checks `revoked` so logout propagates across pods without requiring in-memory invalidation. Rows past `expires_at` are evicted lazily on access and by the rendezvous-partitioned pruner of §14.5 Mode A.\n743\t\n744\t**Redis mode (HA).** For multi-replica Miroir each SQLite table is represented as a Redis keyspace, with the same field semantics:\n745\t\n746\t- `miroir:tasks:<miroir_id>` (hash); list-wide iteration via the set `miroir:tasks:_index`.\n747\t- `miroir:node_settings_version:<index>:<node_id>` (hash); set `miroir:node_settings_version:_index`.\n748\t- `miroir:aliases:<name>` (hash); set `miroir:aliases:_index` backs \"list all\" (§13.7 `GET /_miroir/aliases`).\n749\t- `miroir:session:<session_id>` (hash) with `EXPIRE` matching `session_pinning.ttl_seconds`.\n750\t- `miroir:idemp:<key>` (hash) with `EXPIRE` matching `idempotency.ttl_seconds`.\n751\t- `miroir:jobs:<id>` (hash); queue-depth set `miroir:jobs:_queued` feeds the HPA signal of §14.5.\n752\t- `miroir:lease:<scope>` (string, `SET NX EX 10` renewed every 3s) per §14.5 Mode B.\n753\t- `miroir:canary:<id>` (hash); set `miroir:canary:_index` backs `GET /_miroir/canaries/status`.\n754\t- `miroir:canary_runs:<canary_id>` (sorted set keyed by `ran_at`, value = JSON row); `ZREMRANGEBYRANK` trims to `canary_runner.run_history_per_canary`.\n755\t- `miroir:cdc_cursor:<sink>:<index>` (string, integer seq).\n756\t- `miroir:tenant_map:<sha256_key>` (hash); no secondary index — lookups are always by exact key hash.\n757\t- `miroir:rollover:<name>` (hash); set `miroir:rollover:_index` backs the ILM leader's scan.\n758\t- `miroir:search_ui_config:<index>` (hash).\n759\t- `miroir:search_ui_scoped_key:<index>` (hash, fields `{primary_uid, previous_uid, rotated_at, generation}`); no automatic TTL — state is long-lived until the next rotation. Written by the rotation leader (Mode B, §14.5) and read by every pod on each forwarded SPA request; see §13.21 \"Scoped-key rotation coordination\".\n760\t- `miroir:search_ui_scoped_key_observed:<pod>:<index>` (hash, fields `{generation, observed_at}`) with `EXPIRE` 60s, refreshed on each use of the scoped key. The revocation safety gate reads these keys to decide when every live peer has observed the new generation; see §13.21 \"Revocation safety gate\". The rotation leader-lease itself is already covered by the generic `miroir:lease:<scope>` entry above with scope `search_ui_key_rotation:<index>`.\n761\t- `miroir:admin_session:<session_id>` (hash, fields `{csrf_token, admin_key_hash, created_at, expires_at, revoked, user_agent, source_ip}`) with `EXPIRE` matching `admin_ui.session_ttl_s`. Logout sets `revoked: 1` on the key (kept until `EXPIRE` fires) so every pod's cookie verification re-checks revocation on each request; a Redis Pub/Sub channel `miroir:admin_session:revoked` is additionally notified so in-memory caches can invalidate immediately rather than waiting for the next round-trip.\n762\t- `miroir:ratelimit:searchui:<ip>` (string counter) with `EXPIRE` per `search_ui.rate_limit.redis_ttl_s` (default 60s); bounded by active IP count; see §13.21.\n763\t- `miroir:ratelimit:adminlogin:<ip>` (string counter) with `EXPIRE` 60s; bounded by active attacker IP count. Backs the `POST /_miroir/admin/login` 10/minute-per-IP rate limit when `miroir.replicas > 1`; Helm `values.schema.json` rejects local-only admin-login rate limiting in HA. A companion key `miroir:ratelimit:adminlogin:backoff:<ip>` (hash `{failed_count, next_allowed_at}`) implements the exponential-backoff clause — after 5 consecutive failed attempts the backoff doubles per attempt (10m, 20m, 40m, …) until a valid login resets the counter.\n764\t- `miroir:cdc:overflow:<sink>` (list); bounded by `cdc.buffer.redis_bytes` (default 1 GiB per sink); see §13.13.\n765\t\n766\tTTLs are set on the keyspaces marked above; list-wide queries are served from the `_index` secondary sets so no `SCAN` is required on the hot path. None of the new tables use Redis `EXPIRE` — they are all long-lived configuration or bounded-by-cardinality history.\n767\t\n768\t### Configuration schema\n769\t\n770\t```yaml\n771\tmiroir:\n772\t  master_key: \"\"              # client-facing API key (env: MIROIR_MASTER_KEY)\n773\t  node_master_key: \"\"         # key Miroir uses on nodes (env: MIROIR_NODE_MASTER_KEY)\n774\t  shards: 64\n775\t  replication_factor: 2       # production recommended; Helm chart dev default is 1\n776\t\n777\t  task_store:\n778\t    backend: sqlite            # sqlite | redis\n779\t    path: /data/miroir-tasks.db"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4ebbb998-c656-45b5-9b13-5384c0aa2ecb","uuid":"4238d49e-aeae-4da0-bf7b-daf4b09e12f0","timestamp":"2026-05-13T22:16:04.542Z","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/home/coding/miroir/docs/plan/plan.md","content":"\n### Task store schema (SQLite)\n\nThe task store persists all orchestrator state that must survive a pod restart. In single-replica deployments the backend is SQLite; in HA mode Redis replaces it (keyspace mapping below). Every table below is defined here and cross-referenced from the §13 / §14.5 section that consumes it.\n\n**1. `tasks` — Miroir task registry (defined here; consumed throughout §2, §3, §13).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE tasks (\n    miroir_id   TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n    created_at  INTEGER NOT NULL,\n    status      TEXT NOT NULL,   -- enqueued | processing | succeeded | failed | canceled\n    node_tasks  TEXT NOT NULL,   -- JSON: {\"node-0\": 42, \"node-1\": 17}\n    error       TEXT\n);\n```\n\nBackground Tokio tasks poll node task statuses and update rows. Old tasks are pruned after a TTL (default 7 days) by the rendezvous-partitioned pruner of §14.5 Mode A.\n\n**2. `node_settings_version` — per-(index, node) settings freshness (consumed by §13.5).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE node_settings_version (\n    index_uid   TEXT NOT NULL,\n    node_id     TEXT NOT NULL,\n    version     INTEGER NOT NULL,   -- last cluster-wide settings_version this (index, node) pair verified\n    updated_at  INTEGER NOT NULL,\n    PRIMARY KEY (index_uid, node_id)\n);\n```\n\nAdvanced whenever a two-phase verify (§13.5 Phase 2) or drift-repair cycle succeeds for that pair. Covering-set construction for reads carrying `X-Miroir-Min-Settings-Version` excludes rows where `version < floor`.\n\n**3. `aliases` — atomic index aliases (consumed by §13.7, extended for multi-target by §13.17).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE aliases (\n    name          TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n    kind          TEXT NOT NULL,          -- 'single' | 'multi'\n    current_uid   TEXT,                   -- non-null when kind='single'\n    target_uids   TEXT,                   -- JSON array of UIDs; non-null when kind='multi'\n    version       INTEGER NOT NULL,       -- monotonic flip counter\n    created_at    INTEGER NOT NULL,\n    history       TEXT NOT NULL           -- JSON array: last N prior states, bounded by aliases.history_retention\n);\n```\n\nTwo alias types are supported:\n- **Single-target alias (`kind='single'`)** — one `current_uid`; client writes and reads both resolve to that UID; atomic flip via `PUT /_miroir/aliases/{name}`.\n- **Multi-target alias (`kind='multi'`)** — `target_uids` is a JSON array of concrete UIDs; reads fan out across all of them via §13.11 multi-search and merge by `_rankingScore`; writes are rejected with `miroir_multi_alias_not_writable` (see §13.7). Multi-target aliases are managed exclusively by §13.17 ILM; direct operator edits are refused.\n\nAlias flips update `current_uid` (single) or `target_uids` (multi) and `version` atomically; `history` is append-only within the retention bound.\n\n**4. `sessions` — read-your-writes session pins (consumed by §13.6).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE sessions (\n    session_id            TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n    last_write_mtask_id   TEXT,           -- nullable: session may exist before any write\n    last_write_at         INTEGER,\n    pinned_group          INTEGER,        -- group_id that first reached per-group quorum; nullable when pin cleared\n    min_settings_version  INTEGER NOT NULL,\n    ttl                   INTEGER NOT NULL -- expiry timestamp (ms since epoch); default 15m from last use\n);\n```\n\nLRU-bounded by `session_pinning.max_sessions`. Rows past `ttl` are evicted lazily on access.\n\n**5. `idempotency_cache` — write deduplication (consumed by §13.10).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE idempotency_cache (\n    key              TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n    body_sha256      BLOB NOT NULL,\n    miroir_task_id   TEXT NOT NULL,\n    expires_at       INTEGER NOT NULL\n);\n```\n\nTTL defaults to 24h (`idempotency.ttl_seconds`). LRU-bounded by `idempotency.max_cached_keys`.\n\n**6. `jobs` — work-queued background jobs (consumed by §14.5 Mode C).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE jobs (\n    id                 TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n    type               TEXT NOT NULL,   -- dump_import | reshard_backfill | ...\n    params             TEXT NOT NULL,   -- JSON\n    state              TEXT NOT NULL,   -- queued | in_progress | completed | failed\n    claimed_by         TEXT,            -- pod_id of current claimant; nullable when queued\n    claim_expires_at   INTEGER,         -- lease heartbeat expiry\n    progress           TEXT NOT NULL    -- JSON: { bytes_processed, docs_routed, last_cursor, ... }\n);\n```\n\nClaim semantics and chunking rules are §14.5 Mode C.\n\n**7. `leader_lease` — singleton-coordinator lease (consumed by §14.5 Mode B).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE leader_lease (\n    scope        TEXT PRIMARY KEY,   -- e.g. \"reshard:<index>\", \"alias_flip:<name>\", \"settings_broadcast:<index>\"\n    holder       TEXT NOT NULL,      -- pod_id of current leader\n    expires_at   INTEGER NOT NULL    -- renewed every 3s with a 10s TTL\n);\n```\n\nFor SQLite deployments a single-replica advisory lock substitutes; the row is still written so recovery can read the last committed phase state after leader loss.\n\n**8. `canaries` — canary definitions (consumed by §13.18).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE canaries (\n    id             TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n    name           TEXT NOT NULL,\n    index_uid      TEXT NOT NULL,\n    interval_s     INTEGER NOT NULL,\n    query_json     TEXT NOT NULL,     -- JSON: the canary query body\n    assertions_json TEXT NOT NULL,    -- JSON: array of assertion specs\n    enabled        INTEGER NOT NULL,  -- 0 | 1\n    created_at     INTEGER NOT NULL\n);\n```\n\nCreated and modified via `POST /_miroir/canaries`. The canary runner (Mode A, §14.5) reads this table on each scheduling tick.\n\n**9. `canary_runs` — canary run history (consumed by §13.18).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE canary_runs (\n    canary_id              TEXT NOT NULL,\n    ran_at                 INTEGER NOT NULL,\n    status                 TEXT NOT NULL,    -- pass | fail | error\n    latency_ms             INTEGER NOT NULL,\n    failed_assertions_json TEXT,             -- JSON array or NULL when pass\n    PRIMARY KEY (canary_id, ran_at)\n);\n```\n\nBounded by `canary_runner.run_history_per_canary` (default 100) — older rows are pruned on insert.\n\n**10. `cdc_cursors` — per-sink per-index CDC cursor (consumed by §13.13).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE cdc_cursors (\n    sink_name       TEXT NOT NULL,\n    index_uid       TEXT NOT NULL,\n    last_event_seq  INTEGER NOT NULL,\n    updated_at      INTEGER NOT NULL,\n    PRIMARY KEY (sink_name, index_uid)\n);\n```\n\nAdvanced when a sink ACKs successful delivery of an event batch. `GET /_miroir/changes?since=…` reads against this same monotonic sequence. Shadow-diff state (§13.16) is explicitly **not** persisted — it lives in the in-memory ring buffer of size `shadow.diff_buffer_size`.\n\n**11. `tenant_map` — API-key → tenant mapping for `tenant_affinity.mode: api_key` (consumed by §13.15).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE tenant_map (\n    api_key_hash  BLOB PRIMARY KEY,   -- sha256(api_key)\n    tenant_id     TEXT NOT NULL,\n    group_id      INTEGER             -- nullable: NULL falls through to hash(tenant_id) % RG\n);\n```\n\nLoaded lazily on first request per key and cached per-pod. Only consulted when `tenant_affinity.mode: api_key`.\n\n**12. `rollover_policies` — ILM rollover policies (consumed by §13.17).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE rollover_policies (\n    name           TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n    write_alias    TEXT NOT NULL,\n    read_alias     TEXT NOT NULL,\n    pattern        TEXT NOT NULL,      -- e.g. \"logs-{YYYY-MM-DD}\"\n    triggers_json  TEXT NOT NULL,      -- JSON: { max_docs, max_age, max_size_gb }\n    retention_json TEXT NOT NULL,      -- JSON: { keep_indexes }\n    template_json  TEXT NOT NULL,      -- JSON: { primary_key, settings_ref }\n    enabled        INTEGER NOT NULL    -- 0 | 1\n);\n```\n\nRead by the daily leader-coordinated ILM job (Mode B, §14.5) during each `ilm.check_interval_s` tick.\n\n**13. `search_ui_config` — per-index search-UI configuration (consumed by §13.21).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE search_ui_config (\n    index_uid    TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n    config_json  TEXT NOT NULL,        -- JSON: the `search_ui:` entry as described in §13.21\n    updated_at   INTEGER NOT NULL\n);\n```\n\nWritten by `POST /_miroir/ui/search/{index}/config`; read by the embedded SPA at page-load time.\n\n**14. `admin_sessions` — Admin UI session registry (consumed by §13.19 login/logout, §4 `/_miroir/admin/*`).**\n\n```sql\nCREATE TABLE admin_sessions (\n    session_id      TEXT PRIMARY KEY,\n    csrf_token      TEXT NOT NULL,\n    admin_key_hash  TEXT NOT NULL,    -- sha256 of admin key used at login\n    created_at      INTEGER NOT NULL,\n    expires_at      INTEGER NOT NULL,\n    revoked         INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,\n    user_agent      TEXT,\n    source_ip       TEXT\n);\nCREATE INDEX admin_sessions_expires ON admin_sessions(expires_at);\n```\n\nWritten by `POST /_miroir/admin/login`; `revoked` is flipped to `1` by `POST /_miroir/admin/logout`. Every cookie-authenticated request re-checks `revoked` so logout propagates across pods without requiring in-memory invalidation. Rows past `expires_at` are evicted lazily on access and by the rendezvous-partitioned pruner of §14.5 Mode A.\n\n**Redis mode (HA).** For multi-replica Miroir each SQLite table is represented as a Redis keyspace, with the same field semantics:\n\n- `miroir:tasks:<miroir_id>` (hash); list-wide iteration via the set `miroir:tasks:_index`.\n- `miroir:node_settings_version:<index>:<node_id>` (hash); set `miroir:node_settings_version:_index`.\n- `miroir:aliases:<name>` (hash); set `miroir:aliases:_index` backs \"list all\" (§13.7 `GET /_miroir/aliases`).\n- `miroir:session:<session_id>` (hash) with `EXPIRE` matching `session_pinning.ttl_seconds`.\n- `miroir:idemp:<key>` (hash) with `EXPIRE` matching `idempotency.ttl_seconds`.\n- `miroir:jobs:<id>` (hash); queue-depth set `miroir:jobs:_queued` feeds the HPA signal of §14.5.\n- `miroir:lease:<scope>` (string, `SET NX EX 10` renewed every 3s) per §14.5 Mode B.\n- `miroir:canary:<id>` (hash); set `miroir:canary:_index` backs `GET /_miroir/canaries/status`.\n- `miroir:canary_runs:<canary_id>` (sorted set keyed by `ran_at`, value = JSON row); `ZREMRANGEBYRANK` trims to `canary_runner.run_history_per_canary`.\n- `miroir:cdc_cursor:<sink>:<index>` (string, integer seq).\n- `miroir:tenant_map:<sha256_key>` (hash); no secondary index — lookups are always by exact key hash.\n- `miroir:rollover:<name>` (hash); set `miroir:rollover:_index` backs the ILM leader's scan.\n- `miroir:search_ui_config:<index>` (hash).\n- `miroir:search_ui_scoped_key:<index>` (hash, fields `{primary_uid, previous_uid, rotated_at, generation}`); no automatic TTL — state is long-lived until the next rotation. Written by the rotation leader (Mode B, §14.5) and read by every pod on each forwarded SPA request; see §13.21 \"Scoped-key rotation coordination\".\n- `miroir:search_ui_scoped_key_observed:<pod>:<index>` (hash, fields `{generation, observed_at}`) with `EXPIRE` 60s, refreshed on each use of the scoped key. The revocation safety gate reads these keys to decide when every live peer has observed the new generation; see §13.21 \"Revocation safety gate\". The rotation leader-lease itself is already covered by the generic `miroir:lease:<scope>` entry above with scope `search_ui_key_rotation:<index>`.\n- `miroir:admin_session:<session_id>` (hash, fields `{csrf_token, admin_key_hash, created_at, expires_at, revoked, user_agent, source_ip}`) with `EXPIRE` matching `admin_ui.session_ttl_s`. Logout sets `revoked: 1` on the key (kept until `EXPIRE` fires) so every pod's cookie verification re-checks revocation on each request; a Redis Pub/Sub channel `miroir:admin_session:revoked` is additionally notified so in-memory caches can invalidate immediately rather than waiting for the next round-trip.\n- `miroir:ratelimit:searchui:<ip>` (string counter) with `EXPIRE` per `search_ui.rate_limit.redis_ttl_s` (default 60s); bounded by active IP count; see §13.21.\n- `miroir:ratelimit:adminlogin:<ip>` (string counter) with `EXPIRE` 60s; bounded by active attacker IP count. Backs the `POST /_miroir/admin/login` 10/minute-per-IP rate limit when `miroir.replicas > 1`; Helm `values.schema.json` rejects local-only admin-login rate limiting in HA. A companion key `miroir:ratelimit:adminlogin:backoff:<ip>` (hash `{failed_count, next_allowed_at}`) implements the exponential-backoff clause — after 5 consecutive failed attempts the backoff doubles per attempt (10m, 20m, 40m, …) until a valid login resets the counter.\n- `miroir:cdc:overflow:<sink>` (list); bounded by `cdc.buffer.redis_bytes` (default 1 GiB per sink); see §13.13.\n\nTTLs are set on the keyspaces marked above; list-wide queries are served from the `_index` secondary sets so no `SCAN` is required on the hot path. None of the new tables use Redis `EXPIRE` — they are all long-lived configuration or bounded-by-cardinality history.\n\n### Configuration schema\n\n```yaml\nmiroir:\n  master_key: \"\"              # client-facing API key (env: MIROIR_MASTER_KEY)\n  node_master_key: \"\"         # key Miroir uses on nodes (env: MIROIR_NODE_MASTER_KEY)\n  shards: 64\n  replication_factor: 2       # production recommended; Helm chart dev default is 1\n\n  task_store:\n    backend: sqlite            # sqlite | redis\n    path: /data/miroir-tasks.db","numLines":250,"startLine":530,"totalLines":3740}}}

}\n545\t\n546\t    async fn job_dequeue(&self, worker_id: &str) -> Result<Option<Job>> {\n547\t        // Start a transaction\n548\t        let conn = self\n549\t            .conn\n550\t            .lock()\n551\t            .map_err(|e| TaskStoreError::Internal(e.to_string()))?;\n552\t        let tx = conn.unchecked_transaction()?;\n553\t\n554\t        let now = chrono::Utc::now().timestamp_millis() as u64;\n555\t        let expires_at = now + (5 * 60 * 1000); // 5 minutes from now\n556\t\n557\t        // Find and claim a job\n558\t        let job_id: Option<String> = tx\n559\t            .query_row(\n560\t                \"SELECT id FROM jobs WHERE state = 'queued' ORDER BY id ASC LIMIT 1\",\n561\t                [],\n562\t                |row| row.get(0),\n563\t            )\n564\t            .ok();\n565\t\n566\t        if let Some(ref job_id) = job_id {\n567\t            tx.execute(\n568\t                \"UPDATE jobs SET state = 'in_progress', claimed_by = ?1, claim_expires_at = ?2 WHERE id = ?3\",\n569\t                [\n570\t                    &worker_id as &dyn rusqlite::ToSql,\n571\t                    &expires_at as &dyn rusqlite::ToSql,\n572\t                    job_id as &dyn rusqlite::ToSql,\n573\t                ],\n574\t            )?;\n575\t\n576\t            // Fetch the updated job\n577\t            let job: Job = tx.query_row(\n578\t                \"SELECT id, type, params, state, claimed_by, claim_expires_at, progress\n579\t                 FROM jobs WHERE id = ?1\",\n580\t                [job_id as &dyn rusqlite::ToSql],\n581\t                |row| {\n582\t                    Ok(Job {\n583\t                        id: row.get(0)?,\n584\t                        job_type: row.get(1)?,\n585\t                        params: row.get(2)?,\n586\t                        state: row.get::<_, String>(3)?.parse().map_err(parse_error)?,\n587\t                        claimed_by: {\n588\t                            let claimed: String = row.get(4)?;\n589\t                            if claimed.is_empty() {\n590\t                                None\n591\t                            } else {\n592\t                                Some(claimed)\n593\t                            }\n594\t                        },\n595\t                        claim_expires_at: {\n596\t                            let expires: i64 = row.get(5)?;\n597\t                            if expires == 0 {\n598\t                                None\n599\t                            } else {\n600\t                                Some(expires as u64)\n601\t                            }\n602\t                        },\n603\t                        progress: row.get(6)?,\n604\t                    })\n605\t                },\n606\t            )?;\n607\t\n608\t            tx.commit()?;\n609\t            Ok(Some(job))\n610\t        } else {\n611\t            tx.commit()?;\n612\t            Ok(None)\n613\t        }\n614\t    }\n615\t\n616\t    async fn job_update_status(\n617\t        &self,\n618\t        job_id: &str,\n619\t        status: JobState,\n620\t        result: Option<&str>,\n621\t    ) -> Result<()> &lease.scope as &dyn rusqlite::ToSql,\n739\t                    &lease.holder,\n740\t                    &lease.expires_at,\n741\t                ],\n742\t            )?;\n743\t            true\n744\t std::fmt::Display for ParseError {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> std::fmt::Result {\n        write!(f, \"{}\", self.0)\n    }\n}\n\nimpl std::error::Error for ParseError {}\n\n/// SQLite task store implementation.\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct SqliteTaskStore {\n    conn: Arc<Mutex<Connection>>,\n}\n\nimpl SqliteTaskStore {\n    /// Create a new SQLite task store.\n    pub async fn new<P: AsRef<Path>>(path: P) -> Result<Self> {\n        let conn = Connection::open(path)?;\n        let store = Self {\n            conn: Arc::new(Mutex::new(conn)),\n        };\n        Ok(store)\n    }\n\n    /// Execute a SQL statement with parameters.\n    fn execute(&self, sql: &str, params: &[&dyn rusqlite::ToSql]) -> Result<usize> {\n        let conn = self\n            .conn\n            .lock()\n            .map_err(|e| TaskStoreError::Internal(e.to_string()))?;\n        conn.execute(sql, params).map_err(Into::into)\n    }\n\n    /// Query a single row.\n    fn query_row<T, F>(&self, sql: &str, params: &[&dyn rusqlite::ToSql], f: F) -> Result<T>\n    where\n        F: FnOnce(&rusqlite::Row) -> rusqlite::Result<T>,\n    {\n        let conn = self\n            .conn\n            .lock()\n            .map_err(|e| TaskStoreError::Internal(e.to_string()))?;\n        conn.query_row(sql, params, f).map_err(Into::into)\n    }\n\n    /// Prepare and execute a query, returning all rows.\n    fn query_map<T, F>(&self, sql: &str, params: &[&dyn rusqlite::ToSql], f: F) -> Result<Vec<T>>\n    where\n        F: FnMut(&rusqlite::Row) -> rusqlite::Result<T>,\n    {\n        let conn = self\n            .conn\n            .lock()\n            .map_err(|e| TaskStoreError::Internal(e.to_string()))?;\n        let mut stmt = conn.prepare(sql)?;\n        let rows: std::result::Result<Vec<_>, _> = stmt.query_map(params, f)?.collect();\n        Ok(rows?)\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait::async_trait]\nimpl TaskStore for SqliteTaskStore {\n    async fn initialize(&self) -> Result<()> {\n        let conn = self\n            .conn\n            .lock()\n            .map_err(|e| TaskStoreError::Internal(e.to_string()))?;\n\n        // Enable WAL mode for better concurrency\n        // Use query_row because PRAGMA journal_mode returns the new mode\n        let _mode: String = conn.query_row(\n            \"PRAGMA journal_mode=WAL\",\n            &[] as &[&dyn rusqlite::ToSql],\n            |row| row.get(0),\n        )?;\n\n        // Set busy timeout to avoid deadlock on concurrent writes\n        // Use query_row because PRAGMA busy_timeout returns the value that was set\n        let _timeout: i64 = conn.query_row(\n            \"PRAGMA busy_timeout=5000\",\n            &[] as &[&dyn rusqlite::ToSql],\n            |row| row.get(0),\n        )?;\n\n        // Create schema_version table\n        conn.execute(\n            \"CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS schema_version (\n                version INTEGER NOT NULL\n            )\",\n            &[] as &[&dyn rusqlite::ToSql],\n        )?;\n\n        // Check current version\n        let current_version: Option<i64> = conn\n            .query_row(\n                \"SELECT version FROM schema_version\",\n                &[] as &[&dyn rusqlite::ToSql],\n                |row| row.get(0),\n            )\n            .ok();\n\n        if current_version.is_none() {\n            // Initialize schema\n            Self::init_schema(&conn)?;\n            conn.execute(\n                \"INSERT INTO schema_version (version) VALUES (1)\",\n                &[] as &[&dyn rusqlite::ToSql],\n            )?;\n        } else if current_version != Some(SCHEMA_VERSION) {\n            return Err(TaskStoreError::InvalidData(format!(\n                \"schema version mismatch: expected {}, got {}\",\n                SCHEMA_VERSION,\n                current_version.unwrap()\n            )));\n        }\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    async fn schema_version(&self) -> Result<i64> {\n        self.query_row(\n            \"SELECT version FROM schema_version\",\n            &[] as &[&dyn rusqlite::ToSql],\n            |row| row.get(0),\n        )\n    }\n\n    async created_at, status, node_tasks, error)\n             VALUES (?1, ?2, ?3, ?4, ?5)\",\n            &[\n                &task.miroir_id as &dyn rusqlite::ToSql,\n                &task.created_at,\n                  parse_error(e)\n                        })?,\n                        node_tasks,\n                        error: {\n                            let error: String = row.get(4)?;\n async fn task_update_node(&self, miroir_id: &str, node_id: &str, task_uid: u64) -> Result<()> {\n        // Get the task, update node_tasks (store only task_uid), and write back\n        let mut task &TaskFilter) -> Result<Vec<Task>> {\n        let mut sql =\n            \"SELECT miroir_id, created_at, status, node_tasks, error FROM tasks\".to_string();\n        let mut params = Vec::new();\n        let mut wheres = Vec::new();\n\n        if let Some(status) = filter.status {\n            wheres.push(\"status = ?\".to_string());\n            params.push(status.to_string());\n        }\n\n                    None\n                    } else {\n                        Some(error)\n                    }\n                },\n            })\n        })\n    }\n\n    async fn   )?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    async fn job_dequeue(&self, worker_id: &str) -> Result<Option<Job>> {\n        // Start a transaction\n        let conn = self\n            .conn\n            .lock()\n            .map_err(|e| TaskStoreError::Internal(e.to_string()))?;\n        let tx = conn.unchecked_transaction()?;\n\n        let now = chrono::Utc::now().timestamp_millis() as u64;\n        let expires_at = now + (5 * 60 * 1000); // 5 minutes from now\n\n        // Find and claim a job\n        let job_id: Option<String> = tx\n            .query_row(\n                \"SELECT id FROM jobs WHERE state = 'queued' ORDER BY id ASC LIMIT 1\",\n                [],\n                |row| row.get(0),\n            )\n            .ok();\n\n        if let Some(ref job_id) = job_id {\n            tx.execute(\n                \"UPDATE jobs SET state = 'in_progress', claimed_by = ?1, claim_expires_at = ?2 WHERE id = ?3\",\n                [\n                    &worker_id as &dyn rusqlite::ToSql,\n                    &expires_at as &dyn rusqlite::ToSql,\n                    job_id as &dyn rusqlite::ToSql,\n                ],\n            )?;\n\n            // Fetch the updated job\n            let job: Job = tx.query_row(\n                \"SELECT id, type, params, state, claimed_by, claim_expires_at, progress\n                 FROM jobs WHERE id = ?1\",\n                [job_id as &dyn rusqlite::ToSql],\n                |row| {\n                    Ok(Job {\n                        id: row.get(0)?,\n                        job_type: row.get(1)?,\n                        params: row.get(2)?,\n                        state: row.get::<_, String>(3)?.parse().map_err(parse_error)?,\n                        claimed_by: {\n                            let claimed: String                    }\n                        },\n                        claim_expires_at: {\n                            let expires: i64 = row.get(5)?;\n                            if expires == 0 {\n                                None\n                            } else {\n                                Some(expires as u64)\n                            }\n                        },\n                        progress: row.get(6)?,\n                    })\n                },\n            )?;\n\n            tx.commit()?;\n            Ok(Some(job))\n        } else {\n            tx.commit()?;\n            Ok(None)\n        }\n    }\n\n    async fn job_update_status(\n        &self,\n        job_id: &str,\n        status: JobState,\n        result: Option<&str>,\n    ) -> fn job_list(&self, status: Option<JobState>, limit: usize) -> Result<Vec<Job>> {\n        let mut sql =\n            \"SELECT id, type, params, state, claimed_by, claim_expires_at, progress FROM jobs\"\n                .to_string();\n\n        if status.is_some() {\n            sql.push_str(\" WHERE state = ?\");\n        }\n\n        sql.push_str(&format!(\" ORDER BY id DESC LIMIT Result<bool> {\n        let conn = self\n            .conn\n            .lock()\n            .map_err(|e| TaskStoreError::Internal(e.to_string()))?;\n        let tx = conn.unchecked_transaction()?;\n\n        let now = chrono::Utc::now().timestamp_millis() as u64;\n\n        // Check if there's an existing valid lease for this scope\n        let existing: Option<(String, u64)> = tx\n            .query_row(\n                \"SELECT scope, expires_at FROM leader_lease WHERE scope = ?1 AND expires_at > ?2\",\n                [&lease.scope as &dyn rusqlite::ToSql, &now as &dyn rusqlite::ToSql],\n                |row| Ok((row.get(0)?, row.get(1)?)),\n            )\n            .ok();\n\n        let acquired = if existing.is_some() {\n            false\n        } else {\n            tx.execute(\n                \"INSERT OR REPLACE INTO leader_lease (scope, holder, expires_at)\n                 VALUES (?1, ?2, ?3)\",\n                [\n                    &lease.scope as &dyn rusqlite::ToSql,\n                    &lease.holder,\n                    &lease.expires_at,\n                ],\n            )?;\n            true\n        };\n\n
